Conservative Democrats in the United States Oppose Roosevelt's New Deal; Five Key Figures Telegraph the Convention; But Insufficient to Affect the Election Situation

Philadelphia, USA: Five leaders of the Democratic Party's conservative faction today telegraphed the National Convention delegates, requesting that all those attending the opening session here on Tuesday reject President Roosevelt and his New Deal. Among those listed on the telegram were former New York Governor and 1928 Democratic presidential candidate Al Smith, Secretary of State under President Wilson, Colbert, former Senator Reed, former Massachusetts Governor Ely, and New York Democratic leader Guo Xiang. The telegram urged delegates to work together to eliminate President Roosevelt and his New Deal leaders' control over the party. "Otherwise, voters of all parties will know what to choose to preserve the America created by all the great leaders of the past, and delegates must prevent the abuse of the people's money to purchase the president's propaganda." Democratic leaders today are still optimistic about the prospects for the general election campaign and do not believe that President Roosevelt will lose the support of delegates when the convention is held. However, the actions of Smith and others are also noteworthy, as they show that Smith's relationship with President Roosevelt has been completely severed. Democratic National Committee Chairman and Postmaster General Farley claimed that Smith's telegram was expected and that the purpose of these people is known to everyone. (National Telegram, 21st)

Philadelphia, USA: The Democratic National Convention is scheduled to be held here on June 23. Today, the party's "old guard" leader Smith has begun to issue orders. Smith has long been rumored to be leaving the party, which is further confirmed by the joint declaration issued today by prominent figures on the right wing: Smith, former Massachusetts Governor Ely, former Senator Reed, former Secretary of State Payne Albright, and former Judge Cochlan. The declaration calls for President Roosevelt to be disregarded and replaced by a pure member of the Democratic Party. "If this is not the case, patriotic voters of all parties will certainly know under which banner they should gather to ensure that America has great leaders as in the past." Those in the business community who signed the declaration have not yet been named. This should not be regarded as a major blow to the party. These people may gather some liberals and stand under President Roosevelt's banner. (Reuters, 21st)

Countries That Signed the Treaty of Lausanne Convene in Switzerland to Discuss the Issue of Restoring Military Equipment in the Turkish Straits; Turkey Puts Forward New Proposals

Montreux, Switzerland: Representatives of the signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne met here this afternoon to discuss the issue of restoring military equipment in the Turkish Straits. The Turkish representative suggested that the limit for foreign warships passing through the Straits should be one cruiser and two destroyers, totaling 14,000 tons, or half the tonnage of the Turkish navy. If the Turkish fleet leaves its base, only one vessel should be allowed to pass through at a time. Fleets from Black Sea countries should also be subject to the same restrictions. However, if one of these countries wants to send a 25,000-ton warship into the Black Sea, it should first obtain permission from the Turkish government. The Italian representative did not attend the meeting. It is expected that Italy will send a representative after the League of Nations cancels the sanctions. (Reuters, 21st)

Montreux, Switzerland: The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to hold a meeting at 4:00 PM today. Representatives from eight countries, including Great Britain, France, Japan, Bulgaria, Yugoslavia, Greece, Romania, and the Soviet Union, will attend (Italy did not send representatives). The entire Mediterranean issue may be discussed. As far as the general public knows, the Turkish government will submit a new draft agreement to replace the Treaty of Lausanne. The content is nothing more than four items: Turkey may re-fortify the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits; foreign warships over 14,000 tons are prohibited from passing through the Dardanelles Strait; fleets from non-coastal countries that want to pass through the Straits and enter the Black Sea should be limited to 28,000 tons; Turkish submarines are prohibited from passing through the Straits, and restrictions should also be placed on aircraft flying over the Straits. According to the Treaty of Lausanne in 1923, which Turkey opposes, the north bank of the Dardanelles Strait, which belongs to Europe, must not be fortified, and 12 and a half miles on its south bank, which belongs to Asia, must be designated as a demilitarized zone. The purpose of this treaty is to ensure that, in accordance with "Article 23 of the Treaty of Versailles" (concerning demilitarized zones), ships of all countries can freely pass through the Straits to connect the Mediterranean and Black Sea shipping lanes. (Havas, 22nd)

Montreux, Switzerland: The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to hold a meeting at 4:00 PM today. French representative Former Minister Without Portfolio Peng Gu, British representative Minister of Public Works Lord Stanhope, Soviet representative Commissar for Foreign Affairs Litvinov, Romanian representative Foreign Minister Titulescu, Turkish representative Foreign Minister Rustu, and Yugoslav representative Subotic held preliminary talks this morning to prepare. Well-informed sources believe that the two issues of warships from various countries passing through the Straits and aircraft flying over the Straits will definitely spark heated debates. (Havas, 22nd)

Montreux, Switzerland: The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to meet here today. The representatives of the participating countries are: France is former Minister Without Portfolio Peng Gu, Great Britain is the current Minister of Public Works, former Foreign Minister Lord Stanhope, and Australian Commonwealth Commissioner to the UK Bruce, Turkey is Foreign Minister Rustu, the Soviet Union is Commissar for Foreign Affairs Litvinov, Greece is Ambassador to France Politis, and Bulgaria is Nikolaev. Bruce will be nominated as chairman, and Politis as vice-chairman. According to British sources here, the British government intends to request that discussions be postponed after the opening of the meeting, pending the Extraordinary Congress of the League of Nations passing the abolition of sanctions against Italy this month, so that Italy can also participate in the meeting. At that time, other European issues, such as the Mediterranean issue, can be included on the agenda and discussed together. (Havas, 22nd)

Montreux, Switzerland: The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to meet here today to discuss the issue of restoring fortifications in the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits. The Italian government, which is also one of the signatory countries, notified Turkish Foreign Minister Rustu last night that it would not be able to send representatives to attend, and stated that this move did not conflict with the goals of the meeting. (Havas, 22nd)

Montreux, Switzerland: It has been reported that Italy will not formally participate when the signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne meet here tomorrow, but will only send observers to attend. However, this information has not been confirmed. The meeting is now scheduled to open at 4:00 PM tomorrow. Swiss Federal Government Political Department Minister Mott will attend as the host and deliver the opening speech, and will hold a closed-door meeting on the same day or on Tuesday to formulate the agenda. (Havas, 21st)

Montreux, Switzerland: The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to meet here today. Well-informed sources believe that a misunderstanding has occurred between the Soviet Union and Turkey, the reason being that Turkey may participate in the future Mediterranean Pact, which has caused some concerns in the Soviet Union. (Havas, 22nd)

(Paris) The famous political commentator Dormaison recently wrote an article in Le Figaro, commenting on the attitudes adopted by various countries at the Montreux Conference, stating briefly: "Greece will follow the lead of Great Britain, Yugoslavia will not object to the demands put forward by Turkey, and Romania will be in a difficult position, because after the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits are re-fortified, the country will be confined within the Black Sea and will not be able to cross the line. The situation is the same in Bulgaria, and the inconvenience felt by that country, which has not yet joined the Balkan Consultative Group, is even greater than that of Romania. He also said that the crux of the problem at this time is not the re-fortification of the two straits, but the position of Turkey in the Mediterranean dispute. In other words, what will the country do if war breaks out in the Mediterranean? Therefore, what should be discussed at the Montreux Conference is nominally the issue of the straits, but in reality, it is the issue of the balance of power in the Mediterranean." (Havas, 22nd)

(Paris) The Paris Echo recently published an article by the famous reporter Bertina, commenting on the situation at the Montreux Conference, stating briefly: "If an international treaty like the Treaty of Lausanne in 1923 were to be amended in the past, it would inevitably lead to war, but today, the amendment of the Treaty of Lausanne, the Soviet Union, Turkey, Romania, and Greece are acting in unison. The Turkish government's request to re-fortify the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits will likely be met. However, Bulgaria may take the opportunity to demand access to the Aegean Sea and therefore raise objections. As for Italy, because Turkey, Yugoslavia, and Romania are all Balkan Consultative countries, it may also raise objections. In addition, France and Russia will take the opportunity to hold negotiations with the smaller countries, which is also enough to attract interest, because these smaller countries will definitely try to strengthen the obligations that the major Western European countries should bear towards these smaller countries." (Havas, 22nd)

(London) The signatory countries of the Treaty of Lausanne are scheduled to hold a meeting in Montreux, Switzerland today. The newspapers have recently commented on this matter, generally saying that Turkey's request to re-fortify the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits is very legitimate, but the newspapers do not agree on what attitude the United Kingdom will take towards Turkey's request. According to news from correspondents sent by various newspapers to Montreux, the participating countries, because the Italian-Abyssinian War has now ended, intend to take this opportunity to conduct a comprehensive study of the international situation in the Mediterranean. (Havas, 22nd)

Solar Eclipse Observation: Preliminary Results Released

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Kamishihoro, Dr. Nishina of the Institute of Physical and Chemical Research, who was in the solar eclipse observation team in Hokkaido, observed cosmic rays and announced the relationship between the solar eclipse and cosmic rays on the 21st. According to Dr. Nishina's announcement, there have been two theories about whether cosmic money is affected by solar eclipses or not. The results of the current observation have proven that cosmic rays are not affected by any solar eclipse, that is, cosmic money is not emitted by the sun, nor is it affected by the sun's action. (Domei News Agency, 22nd)

(Moscow) Most of the solar eclipse observation teams believe that the observation results are satisfactory. The plans set by Soviet astronomers and scientific institutions have been largely completed. A complete explanation of the newly obtained materials will still take more time. Soviet astronomers obtained many photographs of the total eclipse. During the two minutes of the total eclipse, natural phenomena were obviously different from usual. The temperature clearly dropped. In Kamchatka, the solar eclipse caused unexpected phenomena. In Kamchatka, landline communication with the mainland was cut off for two hours, and two radios were ineffective at the same time. In addition to 370 Soviet and foreign astronomers, observatories throughout the Soviet Union observed the solar eclipse. (TASS, 22nd)

Turmoil Among the French Right Wing: Not Very Serious and Quickly Subdued

(Paris) After various paramilitary groups were ordered to disband, there was still turmoil in various places last night, but the nature was not very serious and was quickly subdued. The details are as follows:

Tonight at 8:00 PM, members of the youth corps affiliated with various groups formed groups near the Place de l'Étoile and in front of the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, holding tricolor flags and shouting slogans such as "Long live Colonel de la Rocque, leader of the Croix-de-Feu" and "Down with the Jews" (referring to Prime Minister Léon Blum). They marched along the Champs-Élysées for about half an hour and were dispersed by the police, who arrested several demonstrators but released them shortly after.

The Hard News Agency launched a military band concert to entertain the public in the square in front of the Invalides. The military bands lined up and paraded in the Place de la Concorde at 12:45 PM. More than a thousand spectators in the square shouted slogans such as "France belongs to the French." Several people were arrested. At 3:30 PM, there were thousands of people gathered in the Invalides Square, and four excursion cars, carrying many young people, passed through the square shouting slogans such as "Return France to me," "Down with the Soviet Union," and "Down with the Jews." One of them even shouted "Down with Léon Blum" and "Long live the King." Four people were arrested by the police. Soon after, many people created trouble and shouted "Long live Colonel de la Rocque." The police tried their best to suppress them and arrested fifteen people. Order gradually returned. At around 10:00 AM, in front of the "Italy" subway station, vendors of the royalist newspaper "Action Française" and the communist newspaper "L'Humanité" fought each other. At around 11:00 AM, in the "Feuillade" area, more than fifty members of the Croix-de-Feu clashed with members of the Popular Front's left-wing parties. The police persuaded them to disperse and did not arrest anyone.

Colonel de la Rocque, leader of the Croix-de-Feu, yesterday issued a notice to the people of the country to hang the tricolor flag "to express the permanent existence of French national thought." However, in Paris, except for a few areas where wealthy people live, there were very few people hanging the national flag. As for the provinces, according to reports received by the Ministry of the Interior, the number of counties with flags was also very uneven. (Havas, 21st)

(Paris) The strike by department store employees in the capital, with all employees occupying the stores, has lasted for half a month today. Now, after Interior Minister Salengro personally mediated, the labor dispute has been resolved. Employees of the "Lafayette" and "Samaritaine" stores withdrew from the stores at noon, and employees of the "Printemps" store held a final meeting at 5:00 PM. The representatives reported the contents of the agreement reached with the employers. In general, the employees cheered and expressed their satisfaction, and then issued an order to withdraw from the stores. Relatives and friends of the strikers, hearing the news, gathered on Boulevard Haussmann to wait. They saw male and female employees coming out one after another, looking happy and singing the "Printemps" song, which was composed by the store employees during the store occupation. The stores are now scheduled to reopen tomorrow, and the central district of Paris will be able to return to its usual prosperous scene. (Havas, 20th)

(Paris) In the past three days, more than 20,000 striking workers in various industries in the Seine province have resumed work one after another. As of today, the number of strikers nationwide is only 4% of the number during the peak of the labor dispute. (Havas, 21st)

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

General Situation of China's National Wealth and International Relations (3)

— Zhang Qiyun

In the 24th year, the total tonnage of ships entering and leaving China's coastal areas was 10,410,000 tons. Among them, British ships accounted for 42%, Chinese ships accounted for 25%, Japanese ships accounted for 15%, and the rest were the United States, Norway, Germany, the Netherlands, France, Denmark, Portugal, and other countries. The development of highways has been quite rapid in recent years. According to statistics in the 24th year, there are already 90,000 kilometers of highways in the country that are passable by cars. Among them, Guangdong has more than 11,000 kilometers, ranking first in the country, followed by Shandong and Jiangxi with more than 5,000 kilometers each. Others with 2,300 kilometers or more account for more than half of the country. The United States has 48 million kilometers of highways, while China only has 1/400th of that. The United States has one car for every five people on average, the United Kingdom has one car for every 40 people on average, Japan has one car for every 700 people, and China needs 9,000 people to have one car. The gasoline used in our country is all imported, and the import value in recent years is more than 140 million (automobiles and gasoline each account for half). The huge leakage is really shocking. China's civil aviation has three companies: China, Eurasia, and Southwest. The air routes have already exceeded 12,000 kilometers. China Airlines is jointly operated by China and the United States, and Eurasia Airlines is jointly operated by China and Germany, but foreigners only occupy a technical position. Recently, the US Far East Economic Survey Team suggested that the entire US airline establish a trans-Pacific air route, which will shorten the journey from San Francisco to China to four days in the future. In addition, the trans-Eurasian air route from Nanjing via Moscow to Berlin is expected to be reached in only five days. According to statistics from Japan, due to the geographical proximity between China and Japan, the close political and economic relations, and the same culture, postal communication is the most frequent. The total number of postal items received and sent each year is 10 million.

According to the book "China's International Trade Statistics in the Past 65 Years" published by the Academia Sinica, China's international trade ranks 13th in the world, which is not as good as the Netherlands and Belgium. In terms of population ratio, the average trade volume per person is less than three US dollars, which is almost 100 times less than Canada (280 US dollars). China's foreign trade is distributed by region. Before the European War, Central China accounted for one-half, South China accounted for one-quarter, and North China and East China accounted for one-quarter in total. Since the European War, Northeast China has accounted for one-third, Central China has accounted for one-third, and North China and South China have accounted for one-third in total. China's foreign trade is often in deficit, while Northeast China is in surplus. Soybeans, a special product of Northeast China, have always been the largest export commodity in China, which can offset a large part of China's import deficit. The current situation has changed and it is unbearable to recall. According to customs reports, the total value of China's foreign trade in the 24th year was 1.49 billion yuan, of which imports were 920 million yuan and exports were 570 million yuan, resulting in a deficit of 350 million yuan. If the trade value is compared by country, the United Kingdom, Japan, and the United States are the most important, followed by Germany, Russia, and France. Although the status of the United Kingdom itself is behind Japan and the United States, its first position has not been shaken when combined with its colonies. In recent years, a large amount of Indian cotton and Canadian wheat have been imported into China. Hong Kong is a free port, and European goods are transshipped from here, making its position very important. Japan has always ranked first in trade with China (the United Kingdom only counts its own country). After the September 18th Incident, the domestic resistance movement and the disappearance of trade volume in Northeast China have been replaced by the United States. According to the estimation of Professor C.F. Remer of the United States, the capital invested by the powers in China in the 20th year of the Republic of China totaled 3.5 billion yuan (US dollars, including the three northeastern provinces), of which the United Kingdom accounted for 37%, Japan accounted for 35%, and the United States accounted for 6%. The total of these accounts for four-fifths, and the political and economic relations between the three countries and China can be generally seen. Russia's trade with Outer Mongolia and Xinjiang is increasing in importance with each year, but it is not reflected in customs statistics. According to the latest statistics on foreign trade at China's treaty ports in the past 34 years (1900 to 1933) by the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, among the 46 treaty ports in China, the annual trade volume accounts for more than 8% of the total national trade volume, only the five ports of Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Dalian, and Guangzhou. Shanghai's trade has always accounted for more than half of the total national trade volume. According to statistics in the 24th year, Shanghai accounted for 50% of the total national export value and 55% of the total import value. Try to compare Shanghai with Kobe, Japan. In the 23rd year, Kobe's foreign trade volume was 1.58 billion yuan (accounting for 30% of Japan's total trade volume). In the same year, Shanghai's foreign trade volume was 840 million yuan, which means that Kobe surpasses Shanghai and is the number one commercial port in the East. In the same year, there were more than 9,000 foreigners in Kobe, belonging to 44 countries. There were 63,000 foreigners in Shanghai (including 29,000 Japanese, and 10,000 British and Russian each), belonging to 46 countries. From this point of view, Shanghai can be called the number one international metropolis in the East. From this, it can also be seen that China's foreign trade is still largely in the hands of foreigners.

The above description of China's fundamental strength (human and material resources) has shown its general outline. As for the total amount of China's national wealth, there are currently no accurate figures to point to. According to a survey by the Japanese Cabinet Statistics Bureau, Japan's national wealth is 110 billion yuan. Countries with greater wealth than Japan are the United States (880 billion yuan) and the United Kingdom (290 billion yuan). France and Russia are comparable to Japan, and all other countries are below these countries. The estimation of national wealth is extremely difficult. Whether the above estimates are reliable or not is questionable. China's national wealth is not yet known, and it is even more difficult to compare. However, one thing can also reflect China's poverty and weakness, namely primary education. In the 22nd year of the Republic of China, there were more than 17 million elementary school students in Japan (headquarters), that is, 160 elementary school students per thousand people, and the proportion ranked third in the world (after the United States and Australia). According to statistics in the 21st year of our country, there were 11,720,000 elementary school students in the country (the three northeastern provinces are statistics from the previous year), that is, 27 elementary school students per thousand people, which is six times less than Japan. The loss of children is the result of difficult people's livelihood. This shows that people and the land cannot be isolated, and the land cannot be isolated from people. Production and education are closely related and cannot be separated.

Conference of Senior Officers of the Japanese Kwantung Army and the North China Garrison Army - Sakagaki Secretly Arrives in Tianjin to Participate, Important Proposals are Divided into Six Items

Tianjin correspondence, the conference of senior officers jointly held by the Japanese Kwantung Army and the Japanese North China Garrison Army was held in Lüshun on the 18th. To participate in this meeting, Sakagaki Seishiro, Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, took a plane from Jinzhou to Tianjin at 8:30 a.m. on this day. Those who came with him were Konoda, a senior staff officer of the Kwantung Army. Military officers and heads of special service agencies stationed in various parts of North China arrived in Lüshun one day earlier. They gathered at the Japanese Army Headquarters in Haiguang Temple at 9:00 a.m. on this morning. Those present were Japanese Commander Tasiro, Sakagaki, Konoda, and Chief of Staff of the Garrison Army Nagami, Senior Staff Officer Iida, Ishii, Staff Officer Nakai, Lin, Ikeda, Attached Members Matsumuro, Hamada, Senior Adjutant Kawada, Ootake, and heads of various agencies stationed in Yushu Saiki, stationed in Beijing Kazuichi, stationed in Suiha Yosiyama, stationed in Zhang Oomoto, stationed in Tong Yuan Sanyama, Ueno, stationed in Tianjin Matsuoka, etc. In addition, there were military officer Imai stationed in Beiping, military officer Ono stationed in Jinan, military officer Tajiri stationed in Qingdao, etc., a total of more than 40 people. The morning meeting lasted until 12:00 noon for a break, and the afternoon meeting continued at 2:00 p.m. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 p.m. Important proposals include: accelerating the clarification of the Jicha regime; coordinating with the national policy of emphasizing the Sinicization of economic development carried by Ambassador Kawagoe; delimiting the authority of the Kwantung Army and the North China Garrison Army; paying attention to the development of the Southwest Incident, and implementing the military's strategy when necessary; selecting personnel for special organizations and preparing everything in times of emergency; monitoring the actions of the Mayor of Tianjin after he takes office. At 8:00 a.m. on the 19th, senior officials of the two military departments discussed the results of the above-mentioned items in detail to decide on implementation. Military officers and heads of special service agencies in various places have left Tianjin and returned to their posts one after another since the evening of the 18th. Sakagaki's trip to Tianjin was the most secretive. The Japanese military denied his arrival, so it was not known whether he had left Tianjin and returned to Changchun as of the 19th. However, Imai, Deputy Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, did come to Tianjin from Changchun by plane at 11:00 a.m. on the 19th, accompanied by Staff Officer Hanatani. On the same day, he held a small secret meeting with Tasiro, Nagami, Matsumuro, Iida, and others, stayed in Tianjin for three or four days, went to Tongzhou in Beiping, and then flew to Zhangbei for inspection. He will return to Changchun via Jehol on the 28th. At 2:30 p.m. on the 19th, Ishii, a senior staff officer of the Japanese North China Garrison Army, gave a speech to reporters, saying, "After Chairman Song arrived in Lüshun, he went to Zhang Tuan's residence with Chen Juesheng, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, at 4:00 p.m. on the 18th to visit Commander Tasiro. This was the first meeting between Tasiro and Zhu since he took office. They talked for about an hour and then left. Diplomatic matters were not discussed in depth because it was the first meeting. Recently, the Jicha Political Council has not sent anyone to contact us on such matters. There is no such thing as Japan continuing to increase troops in North China. According to Hamada, attached to the army in Beiping, he did not deny this, saying that the new team could arrive in mid-July." Beiping plans to increase the current number of people by two times. The troops that came here earlier have no barracks to live in, so they camp along the Beining Railway line. They will leave after the barracks are completed. It is not that troops are being transferred from the country again. At yesterday's (18th) military conference, some people suspected that the Japanese army would have further plans for North China. However, both the former and current commanders are eager for peace and prosperity in North China, and for the people to live and work in peace. Japan has no intention of using troops against North China. This is evidenced by the fact that the military has helped to quell the rebellion of Bai Jianwu last year. Currently, there are many rumors, most of which are fabricated by disgruntled people who collude with rogues and want to take advantage of the opportunity. The military is now paying attention. The authority of the Kwantung Army and the North China Garrison Army is usually bounded by the Great Wall, but sometimes they do not distinguish between regions and adopt close liaison. The Japanese army is directly subordinate to the Emperor, just like an electric light. When the "button" is twisted, the whole thing is bright. Therefore, the Kwantung Army's planes can be dispatched into the Guan by the North China Military Department at any time. The Jidong area is under the responsibility of the North China Military Department. However, if the incident involves diplomacy, the Kwantung Army also has the right to intervene."

Palace Museum Theft Case - Suspect Apprehended

Guarding Team Soldiers Arrested and Lost Items Recovered

Beiping correspondence, the second theft case was discovered in the Palace Museum in Beiping a few days ago. After strict investigation by the authorities, it is expected that the whole case will be clarified within a few days. According to the announcement of the Palace Museum yesterday, the Public Security Bureau sent personnel to take fingerprints of the soldiers and laborers of each team in the hospital at the beginning of the discovery of this case, and no one was allowed to ask for leave. On the morning of the 19th, Zhao Boyan, a soldier of the Guarding Team, and Zhao Shengfu, a laborer (that is, Zhao Boyan's father), were found not to be working in the hospital. After sending personnel to inquire, it was discovered that the Zhao family and his son had abandoned their homes and fled. On the same day, Zhuang Shangyan, a section chief of the hospital, found paintings and calligraphy by Mian Ning and Na Yanbao at Shuangjuhe Antique Shop at No. 217, Dajie outside the back gate, which matched the register of those stolen this time. He went to the shop on the pretext of buying antique fans. The shop took out two fan faces and one similar one. Then the hospital, together with the district police, went to the shop to search and found three old bone folding fans. The hospital, together with the procurators of the two local courts, sent Zhang Yongquan, the shopkeeper of the shop, Zhang Dechen, the young shopkeeper of Ronghua Zhai, the guarantor of Zhao Boyan, Wang Zhao, Zhao Boyan's sister, and Li Yirong, the shopkeeper of Xicheng Shun Shop, the guarantor of Zhao Shengfu, to the court for interrogation.

On the 20th, Zhuang Shangyan went to inquire around the back gate inside and outside. Pinggu Zhai Antique Shop voluntarily handed over 14 paintings and calligraphy by Mian Ning, Mian Yi, Na Yanbao, Wang Chengpei, and Shen Huan. Li Guangge Antique Shop also voluntarily handed over seven pieces. According to them, these fan faces were all bought from Wang Xu, a resident outside the back gate. Wang Xu was also one of the soldiers of the Palace Guarding Team. He was arrested together with the district police. After a brief interrogation, he confessed to stealing the treasures. According to Wang Xu's confession, when he was on duty in Qianqing Palace two months ago, he asked his companion Zhao Boyan to guard him while he went to the toilet. When he returned, he saw Zhao walking out from behind the throne. After questioning, he responded vaguely and said that he wanted to report it. Zhao then confessed to stealing the treasures, repeatedly begged Wang to be tolerant, and asked Wang to go to Zhao's house after get off work. Zhao gave Wang an enamel watch, a painting core, and eight fans. When Wang took it home, Wang's mother ordered him to return it or sell it quickly. Wang sold the watch to Cheng Xingyun Antique Shop outside the back gate and got 21 yuan. He sold the fans to Pinggu Zhai and got 23 yuan. The painting core (that is, Zhao Ziang's Painting Horse) was also sold to Cheng Xingyun for one yuan.

On the 21st, Liu, Zhao Boyan's wife, was arrested on Di'anmen Street. According to her confession, Zhao Shengfu, my father-in-law, said yesterday, you should quickly find your husband and run away. My husband, Zhao Boyan, was either inside Deshengmen. I went into the city to find him, but I couldn't find him. After I went home, he and his son had already fled. According to Qi Changshuo, a shop assistant at Pinggu Zhai, the seller of antiques was surnamed Wang, wearing leather shoes and a Serge coat. When he came to sell for the second time, there was still a painting core that he didn't buy. According to the shop assistant of Li Guangge, the seller of antiques was surnamed Wang, in his twenties. Zhao Ziang's Painting Horse had three horses and two people. Because it was a rough silk ground, he didn't want it. According to people involved, the antiques stolen from the Palace Museum this time also include treasures such as white jade cabbage, jade coral, and large and small Ruyi. These are all guarded by police officers on patrol in turns, and it is quite difficult to steal them. This theft may have occurred when wearing leather cotton clothes in winter and spring, and they were carried out in their arms. Currently, the Palace Museum and the court are still conducting strict investigations separately, and they are trying to find out the truth of the whole case within a few days. (21st)

Liu Guitang Assassinated in Tianjin - Three Bullets in the Head and Chest, Not Dead, the Reason for the Assassination Has Not Been Determined

Tianjin correspondence, since last winter and this spring, Liu Guitang gathered more than 2,000 bandits Wang Hanru, Wang Daoyi, Zhang Haijiao, etc., and went south from the Changcheng Line in Chahar, following the old path of the 23rd year, wanting to return to the junction of Henan, Shandong, and Hebei to occupy. After being intercepted and defeated by the garrisons, most of them returned to Siyihaiye and Yongning Fort in eastern Chahar, under the command of Wang Daoyi. They were recruited and reorganized into security teams by the Chahar Provincial Government. However, because they were difficult to tame, they fought with the security teams Feng Shoupeng and Luo Zi's troops a month ago and were resolved by the joint efforts of Feng and Luo. The remaining troops were led by Li Ziying and fled outside the Great Wall, collapsing along the border wall and joining forces with Zhang Haijiao's scattered bandits. They roamed along the various passes of the Great Wall. Liu himself escaped to Tianjin from eastern Shandong in early spring and hid in a rented house in Gengyuli 1, Akashi Street, Japanese Concession. Many of his old subordinates lived with him. Because Liu was unwilling to be lonely, he has been trying to rise again for several months. Recently, because the situation in North China is bad, all the disgruntled warlords and politicians are thinking of moving. Liu then united with a certain inspector and a certain commander-in-chief, wanting to gather his diehards to rebel. His chief of staff, Jin Huanwen, was also ordered to go to the Malan Pass area to contact Zhang Haijiao and others, intending to wait for the opportunity to act. At 10:20 p.m. on the 20th, two people suddenly came to Liu's residence and knocked on the door. The gatekeeper of Liu's residence opened the door and came out to see. The two people claimed to be Liu's subordinates. The gatekeeper found that one of them seemed to be surnamed Zhang, who had served as a regimental commander in Sun Chuanfang's army and often came to Liu's residence to visit Liu and talk. Although he did not know the name of the other person, he also felt that his face was familiar. He immediately invited them into the gatehouse and asked them to wait. The gatehouse was the south room downstairs, and Liu's subordinates lived downstairs in the north, with several people playing mahjong. Liu himself came downstairs to sit and watch. The two people who claimed to be Liu's subordinates did not wait for permission and broke into the north downstairs, drew their guns and fired six or seven shots at Liu. Three bullets hit Liu's left chest near the armpit, and all the bullets went through. One bullet hit Liu's left lower jaw and went through his right cheek. A servant of his was also hit in the waist by a bullet. They both fell to the ground. After the two attackers succeeded, they took advantage of the crowd's panic and jumped over the short wall to escape, running through the alley after Gengyuli and rushing to the corner of Suma Street to board a car that was waiting there. When Liu's family saw something happen, they immediately reported to the Japanese police station. Immediately, Ikeue, the captain of the Japanese gendarmerie detachment, and Oowa, the director of the Judicial Department of the police station, led the military police to the investigation. The entire Japanese Concession was immediately under alert. Akashi, Fukushima, and Suma Streets were temporarily cut off from traffic to search for the criminals, but nothing was found. Liu and the servant were carried to the Gongwen Hospital for treatment. That night, they could not speak due to excessive bleeding. The servant was only slightly injured and was fine. On the morning of the 21st, Liu fainted once. Later, he was resuscitated with a cardiac stimulant injection. Around noon, Oowa, the director of the Japanese police station, went to the hospital to investigate. Liu was already able to speak. The treatment was progressing well. According to reports, the reason for the assassination is still unclear. However, a servant surnamed Xu in his entourage disappeared after the incident. It is suspected that he was bought by someone and colluded with foreigners to carry out the assassination. Gongli Hospital determined that Liu needed to rest for two months before he could recover. The Japanese police station and the gendarmerie detachment did not withdraw the alert on Akashi Street on the 21st and were still searching for the criminals. After this incident occurred, all those with ambitions and plans to act have rushed to a certain party since the night of the 20th to beg for protection in order to prevent accidents. (21st)

New Appointed Chairman of Chahar Province, Liu Ruming, Arrives in Zhangjiakou to Assume Office

Guo Zhihan Represents Song to Oversee the Handover, Liu Proposes Four Points for Self-Encouragement

Zhangjiakou Correspondence: The newly appointed Acting Chairman of the Chahar Provincial Government, Liu Ruming, arrived in Zhangjiakou from Beiping on the 20th. At 10:00 AM on the 21st, the inauguration ceremony was held. Attendees included Guo Zhihan, representative of the Chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Commission; Yao Jingchuan, Commander of the Second Cavalry Brigade; representatives from various departments, commissions, organizations, and groups; Nakané, the Japanese Consul-General stationed in Zhangjiakou; and Oomoto, Chief of the Special Affairs Agency; totaling over 300 people. After the meeting began, the entire assembly bowed three times to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, and sang the Party song. First, the outgoing Chairman Zhang Zizhong, represented by Yang Zhaogeng, gave an account and a speech, briefly stating that Chairman Zhang had been transferred to head Tianjin Municipality, and because he had just taken office and was busy with duties, he could not come to Zhangjiakou in person, so he sent him as a representative to handle all handover matters. After Yang finished speaking, the seal handover ceremony was held. Then, Guo Zhihan delivered an instructional speech, briefly stating, "Today is the day Chairman Liu assumes office as acting chairman. I am very honored to be here on behalf of Chairman Song. Everyone knows that Chairman Liu has made outstanding achievements in the past and has made great contributions in politics and is greatly concerned about national affairs. Liu himself has been stationed in Chahar Province for a long time and is very familiar with the situation in Chahar. This time, Chairman Song specially appointed him to act as Chairman of Chahar Province, which is certainly a pleasant and competent appointment. I hope for three things in actively building and stabilizing the people: First, Chahar is in a state of decay after years of chaos. In the future, we should act in accordance with the principle of pleasing the people and eliminating what they dislike, so that the people can be stable and the local area can be prosperous. Second, uphold integrity. This is what officials must abide by, and it is even more necessary in a turbulent national state. In the future, we should act positively in accordance with the two words 'integrity' to realize a clean and honest provincial government. Third, value diplomatic relations. Chahar Province, under the current circumstances, should abide by the national government's order of good neighborliness and work with sincerity and courtesy on the principle of equality and mutual benefit, and embark on the path of peace." After Guo finished speaking, Liu Ruming gave a response, briefly stating, "Distinguished guests, comrades, I have been ordered to concurrently serve as acting Chairman of Chahar Province. Today I am assuming office, and I am deeply honored by the warm participation of Director Guo sent by Chairman Song and all the guests. I have been serving in the military and am not very familiar with local conditions. I am afraid that I will not be able to fulfill this role. I can only follow the instructions of Chairman Song, the established rules of former Chairman Zhang, and the efforts of all my colleagues to move forward, perhaps achieving some results within the scope of possibility. Now, I have four points for self-encouragement in political affairs: First, to defend public security, I will vow to supervise the military and police and work hard to suppress bandits, stabilize the local area, and let the people live and work in peace. Second, to strive to fulfill my responsibilities, follow the achievements of Chairman Zhang in the past, lead civil servants to eliminate malpractices, and actively move towards the right track. Third, to strictly prohibit the Communist bandits. The Communist bandits kill and set fires everywhere, spreading misfortune to young people, and there is a great hidden danger. In the future, the Chahar Provincial Government must strictly ban them to ensure that no bandits are found within the territory, so as not to endanger the foundation of the country. Fourth, to abide by the central government's repeated orders of good neighborliness and implement good diplomatic relations. The Chahar Provincial Government will adhere to this purpose and work sincerely to maintain peace in East Asia. These four points are relatively major, so they are specifically put forward. There are also many other common situations, which must be handled according to local conditions. I hope that you will provide corrections at any time, which is what I hope for." After Liu finished his response, photos were taken and the ceremony was announced complete. It was half-past ten. For the sake of camaraderie, Liu hosted a banquet for Guo Zhihan and the heads of various departments in the provincial government at 11:00 AM, which lasted until noon before everyone happily dispersed.

After assuming office, Liu Ruming told reporters, "The original Secretary-General of the Provincial Government, Ma Yanchong, has gone to Tianjin to take office with former Chairman Zhang. I have submitted a recommendation to the Political Affairs Committee for the successor, which will be officially announced in a few days. The various departments and offices of the Provincial Government will take over this afternoon (the 21st), and there will be no major changes in personnel. I will go to Beiping around the 24th, then go to Tianjin to meet Chairman Song, report on the inauguration, and make some requests." (21st)

Discussion on the Implementation Plan of National Economic Construction (Part 2)

– Zhu Ping

5. Organization of National Economic Construction

According to the current national defense situation and the stage of economic development in our country, the organization of national economic construction should take the county as the basic regional unit, with the province and the central government responsible for planning, adjustment, guidance, and supervision. Economic construction matters that fall within the scope of the whole country or the whole province will be planned and promoted directly by the central government and the province. The following is a draft of the organizational outline for each level:

A. Central Organs

The central government shall establish a Central National Economic Construction Committee.

The committee shall establish four departments: Secretariat, Planning, Guidance, and Assessment. The Planning Department shall establish groups for investigation, statistics, labor, land, finance, production, consumption, trade, prices, transportation, and culture and defense. The directors and members of each group shall be appointed by the committee from appropriate personnel from the central party and government and cultural institutions.

Under the committee, various specialized committees shall be established according to the classification of industries, and shall be composed of ministers or vice-ministers of the relevant departments of the Executive Yuan, as well as domestic economic and technical experts.

The Central National Economic Construction Committee shall be responsible for the planning, adjustment, guidance, and assessment of national economic construction. Economic construction matters that should be directly undertaken by the central government shall be handled by the original competent administrative organs of the central government.

The organizational rules of the Central National Economic Construction Committee and its affiliated organs shall be determined separately.

The expenses of the committee shall be covered by the central government, except for the salaries of the personnel transferred from various organs, which shall be paid by their respective organs.

B. Provincial Organs

Each province shall establish a Provincial National Economic Construction Committee.

The organization of the affiliated organs under the Provincial Committee shall be the same as that of the central government.

The Provincial Committee shall be responsible for the planning, adjustment, guidance, and assessment of economic construction in the province. Economic construction matters that should be directly undertaken by the province shall be handled by the original competent provincial administrative organs by the committee.

The organizational rules of the Provincial Committee and its affiliated organs shall be determined separately.

Cities and districts equivalent to provinces shall have the same organization as provinces.

The expenses for the Provincial Committee to handle business shall be covered by the provincial government.

C. County Organs

The county shall establish a County Economic Construction Committee.

The County Committee shall establish groups for Secretariat, Planning, Organization and Guidance, and Assessment. The directors of each group shall be concurrently held by committee members, and the members shall be transferred from the county party, government, and cultural institutions by the committee.

The tasks of the County Committee are as follows:

1. Investigate the economic conditions in the county and report them to the Provincial Committee on time.

2. Determine the economic construction plan of the county and supervise its implementation.

3. Execute the orders of the province and the central government regarding economic construction matters in the county.

4. Organize trade associations and village agricultural associations in the county, and guide and supervise their work.

5. Approve the economic construction or production plans of various industries and supervise their implementation.

6. Remove various obstacles to the economic development of various industries.

7. Supervise the implementation of the control of import and export goods.

8. Adjust labor-capital relations.

9. Guide various industries on technical, operational, and organizational improvements.

10. Adjust the mutual relations between various industries.

11. Manage the storage and distribution of food throughout the county.

12. Supervise the activities of financial organizations throughout the county.

The organization of the County Committee shall be determined separately.

The expenses of the County Committee shall be covered by the county government.

D. Town and City Trade Associations

Each basic unit of industry, commerce, transportation, and culture in each town and city shall organize various trade associations according to their respective professional categories.

Various trade associations shall also jointly organize a federation of trade associations.

Each trade association shall be organized under the guidance of personnel dispatched by the County Economic Construction Committee. All units in the same town or city in the same profession must join the trade association of that town or city.

The chairman of each trade association shall be elected by the members from three candidates nominated and submitted to the County Committee for approval.

The expenses of each trade association shall be shared by the members. If insufficient, the government may be requested to provide subsidies.

The tasks of the trade associations:

1. To do its best to solve the difficulties in the business of its members, and to adjust their mutual relations, so that they can help each other to develop their entire enterprise.

2. To report the business conditions of various industries to the County Economic Construction Committee on a regular basis, and to submit the economic construction plan of the industry to the County Committee.

3. To execute the parts of the county's economic construction plan related to the industry according to the orders of the County Committee.

After the formation of each trade association, it may request economic and technical assistance from the government with the approval of the County Committee.

E. Village Agricultural Associations

Any village with more than 100 farming households must organize a village agricultural association. Villages with fewer than 100 households may combine several villages to form one. Its work shall be guided by personnel dispatched by the County Committee from time to time.

The chairman of the village agricultural association shall be elected by the representatives of the farming households in the village from three candidates nominated by the County Committee.

The operating expenses of the village agricultural association shall be borne by the members. If insufficient, the government may be requested to provide subsidies.

Farmers who join the village agricultural association must report the management and operation of their farming, as well as various facts about agricultural economics, to the village agricultural association in detail, and formulate an annual and quarterly production plan within the prescribed period every year and every quarter.

The tasks of the village agricultural association:

1. To investigate the agricultural conditions in the village and submit the village's "production plan" to the County Committee.

2. To solve the production problems of members and adjust their mutual relations.

3. To execute the orders of the County Committee.

4. To accept the guidance of the County Committee and implement agricultural technology, improved silkworm eggs, fertilizers, and by-product manufacturing, and engage in water conservancy and disaster prevention facilities.

5. To cooperate in seeking the development of credit organizations and improve the original debt situation of members.

Local News

New Japanese Ambassador, Shigeru Kawagoe, Arrives in Shanghai from Japan - Issues Written Statement Aboard Ship - Hopes Chinese Friends Will Assist in Opening Up Relations Between the Two Countries - Strengthen People's Ties to Ensure Peace in East Asia

New Japanese Ambassador

The newly appointed Japanese Ambassador to China, Shigeru Kawagoe, along with his wife and secretary Hoshida, arrived in China aboard the Asama Maru to assume his new post. The ship was delayed due to encountering a storm en route and did not arrive at the Huishan Wharf until 2:40 PM. The wharf area was guarded by armed police officers dispatched by the Public Concession Police Department and the Japanese Embassy Police Department. Chinese and Japanese individuals who came to the port to welcome him included Zhou Jue and his wife, director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office; Wang Changchun, representing Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Xu Xiuzhi, former Vice Minister of the Interior and friend of Ambassador Kawagoe; banker Zhou Zuomin; journalists Hu Zhengzhi and Zhang Jiluan; and from the Japanese side, Minister Wakasugi Kaname of the Embassy; Naval Attaché Sato, Lieutenant General, and Attaché Okino; Army Attaché Kiita, Major General, and Attaché Utsunomiya; Counselors Arino, Horiuchi, and Honno; and all personnel from the Japanese Embassy and Consulate General; and Gan'nou, Chairman of the Japanese Residents' Association, Miri, and over a hundred others. Ambassador Kawagoe shook hands with each of the Chinese and Japanese welcomers and then met with the Chinese and foreign press aboard the ship before taking a car to the ambassadorial residence on Bisson Road to rest.

Written Statement

When Ambassador Kawagoe arrived in Shanghai, he issued a statement in Chinese, English, and Japanese, saying, "I feel a great responsibility to come to China this time on assignment. Fortunately, like my predecessors, Ambassadors Arita and Ariyoshi, I have been involved in matters related to China both domestically and internationally for quite some time, and I have many friends in the north and south of China. Therefore, I intend to rely on the strength of these old friends and acquaintances in order to do my best to open up relations between China and Japan. The current difficulties facing China are complex and diverse, among which the development of the national economy is particularly urgent. Japan sincerely hopes to cooperate with China in developing its economy. Needless to say, I intend to rely on the aforementioned cooperation between China and Japan to strengthen the ties between the people of the two countries, to promote good neighborly relations between the two countries, and to ensure peace in East Asia. I sincerely hope that all parties will provide assistance to me so that I can accomplish my mission."

Appearance and Demeanor

Ambassador Kawagoe is 56 years old. He graduated from Tokyo Imperial University and served in the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, where he was successively assigned to the Japanese Embassy in Germany and other places. He was transferred to serve as Consul General in Qingdao, Guangzhou, Jilin, Tianjin, and other places. He has been in China for more than ten years. After former Ambassador to China Arita was promoted to Foreign Minister, Kawagoe was promoted from Consul General in Tianjin to Ambassador to China. When Kawagoe arrived in Shanghai yesterday, he was wearing a gray suit and black leather shoes. His hair was slightly graying, but he looked energetic. His wife was of a similar age and interacted with the Chinese and Japanese welcomers with a generous demeanor.

Date of Trip to Nanjing

According to Arino, a counselor at the Japanese Embassy, who spoke to a Central News Agency reporter aboard the ship, the new ambassador will meet with Japanese expatriates in Shanghai and personnel from the embassy and consulates after arriving in Shanghai, and the date of his trip to Nanjing to present his credentials has not yet been officially announced, so it has not been decided. However, it is already being discussed and is scheduled for 11:00 AM on the 30th of this month. If it is confirmed, the ambassador will enter Nanjing on the evening of the 28th and first meet with Foreign Minister Zhang. Regarding the question of the embassy's relocation to the south, since an office has been established in the capital, the ambassador will be permanently stationed in Nanjing and Shanghai, and it seems that it can be postponed. Shanghai news on the 22nd from the League of Nations stated that Ambassador Kawagoe, who arrived in Shanghai today, will begin tomorrow to receive reports on the local situation from Councilor Wakasugi, Consul General Suma in Nanjing, and the military and naval attachés, and will also convey the central government's policy. He is scheduled to depart Shanghai on the 28th with the military and naval attachés and embassy staff, arrive in Nanjing on the 29th, and present his credentials on the 30th.

Sir Otto Niemeyer's Farewell Remarks: Hosted Journalists Yesterday Afternoon, Departing China by Ship Today

Sir Otto Niemeyer, the British economic advisor, came to China last autumn and visited Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, Guangdong, Wuhan, and other places to investigate China's economic situation. He also visited Japan again at the end of last month to meet with Japanese authorities and exchange views. He returned to Shanghai a few days ago and will depart China today at 4 PM on the British Company's *Rempura* with his wife and assistant, Messrs. Paget and Rogers. Sir Otto visited Minister of Finance Kong yesterday to say goodbye and met with journalists at the Cathay Hotel at 4 PM to deliver the following remarks:

The British government sent me to investigate China's financial and economic difficulties and the possibility of our allied powers assisting China in overcoming these difficulties. I have been in China for almost nine months and have diligently and humbly investigated the situation in China. A large portion of my time, due to practical needs, was spent in Shanghai, but I also traveled to Nanjing, Tianjin, Beijing, Hankou, Chongqing, Xiamen, and Guangzhou, and met with representatives of the government authorities and banking and business circles in various places. The British government originally hoped that the United States, Japan, and France would each send experts to cooperate with me, but this did not materialize. However, the United States recently sent an important economic survey mission to China, and I have read their report with great interest. I have been in contact with representatives of the Japanese government and bankers in Shanghai and have traveled to Tokyo twice to gain a clear understanding of the Japanese government's views. My detailed report on this trip will be submitted to my government in the future. However, it would be beneficial to briefly describe my impressions before leaving China. The first problem I noticed was, of course, the position of currency. Silver has been China's currency for many centuries. In 1934, the sudden surge in silver prices caused the exchange rate of China's currency to rise accordingly. Compared to world prices, Chinese products became very expensive, leading to a decrease in exports. China had to export silver to offset the unfavorable balance of international trade. As a result, credit declined, forming a deflationary trend. Domestic prices fell, creditors could not recover debts, and banks stored silver in their vaults without being able to use it. The decline of the Shanghai real estate industry further aggravated the situation. In October 1934, the Chinese government, recognizing the severity of the crisis, issued an order to levy an export tax on silver. As a result, the Shanghai silver dollar became isolated from the free silver standard. However, while this measure was sufficient to reduce the extreme impact of rising silver prices, it still failed to eliminate the underlying difficulties. When I arrived in Shanghai last September, it was necessary to take more positive steps. China was abandoning the silver standard at this time, but had not adopted another monetary system. My arrival in China did not bring any definite plan to invite the Chinese government to adopt, because at that time there was more than one way to adopt, and the decision of which to choose was greatly related to the psychology of the Chinese people. At that time, only the Chinese government could decide. At that time, I examined the monetary situation and drafted a detailed plan to ensure safety as the main requirement. If possible, I also sought international assistance. However, before this plan was completed, the exchange rate became weaker and weaker, and the government had to adopt the legal tender control policy based on its own strength. I am not responsible for this bold step, but the success of this policy shows that it is indeed beneficial. After the new currency was issued, it was circulated throughout the country without much difficulty. The legal tender issued by the government bank gradually replaced the silver dollar in the market, and its exchange rate remained fixed. At the same time, the government's ability to maintain this exchange rate also increased sufficiently. The exchange rate set by the government promoted exports on the one hand, and the increase in agricultural prices on the other hand, the purchasing power of farmers also improved. The unfavorable balance of international trade was greatly reduced, and the balance of international payments has been achieved. Therefore, the basic economic needs for consolidating the currency have been successful. I think the progress of the Chinese government's monetary policy is indeed worth celebrating. The Chinese government has achieved a lot of success in financial and economic recovery. The people's faith in currency is becoming increasingly solid, but in order to obtain a reliable basis for long-term trade and investment plans, it is still necessary to succeed in other steps. Because the government's implementation of new policies did not have a long-term announcement in advance, the various steps had to be implemented one by one. If the unified issuance of legal tender and the reorganization of the central bank have not been implemented yet, non-commercial speculative behavior will also make people feel uneasy. The government's budget is in deficit and borrowing is unavoidable. The domestic debt market is weak and sluggish, and the government's credit is also weak. Although the financial market is now more relaxed, many commercial banks have still failed to be active. In addition, the political difficulties in North China and South China, and the recent plunge in silver prices after the United States stopped buying silver in the world market, are all points of difficulty. However, on the whole, if the Chinese government can complete its domestic improvement plan, especially focusing on the reorganization of the central bank and the reform of the budget, then it can be completely trusted in the economic aspect. The future of China's currency and even the entire financial position in the future must first depend on the maintenance of domestic security in China, and second, must be based on the resolution of the special situation in North China. China's customs duties are most concerned in finance. Therefore, the difficulties in tax collection in eastern Hebei should be urgently sought for decision-making. However, if you want to solve this difficulty, you must first seek political understanding between China and Japan to be successful. When I was in Tokyo, the Japanese authorities stated that Japan also hoped for this understanding, advocating the integrity of China's tax administration, never supporting local authorities to split the customs administration or establish independent tax regulations, and even less willing to interfere in China's internal affairs. Therefore, I sincerely hope that the current difficulties can be resolved to restore general trust and promote investment and trade activities. I pay close attention to the issue of currency, because the consolidation of finance is the basis of trade. If the exchange rate fluctuates, credit will be tightened and trade will be difficult. However, after the currency is consolidated, other aspects should be used to promote exports. Plans, such as reducing domestic tax rates, improving the quality of goods, and improving management and design, etc. However, it seems that China's natural exports should be controlled to a lesser extent. As for imports, there will be no immediate progress, because the progress of the import industry is a prerequisite for the progress of the export industry. I hope that when the opportunity comes in the future, British exporters will be able to take advantage of the opportunity to seek development. More importantly, the rise and fall of the import industry depends on the level of tax rates. I hope the Chinese government can consider the point that we can still reduce tax rates without reducing tax revenue. Recently, some tax rates are too high. As a result, they only make importers wait and see, and tax revenues also suffer losses. I think the setting of tax rules should be revised with the current exchange rate as the standard. In terms of industry, it is hoped that the high tax rate will be maintained, but for farmers, the high import tax is really afraid that it will be harmful and unprofitable. Therefore, the government's responsibility is to make both parties reach a balance, and from the current situation, it is more important to restore Chinese agriculture than to revitalize industry. Therefore, in my personal opinion, if the import tax rate can be reduced, it will be beneficial to China in both financial and economic terms. China's development depends heavily on the import of some important goods. This is probably the most promising point for British exporters. In the past, Britain provided a lot of assistance to China's railways. Unfortunately, China's debt credit has not been repaid as scheduled, resulting in failure to obtain new loans. Now the Chinese government is determined to repay old debts to the extent of its financial capacity, and has also made many improvements in railway management. Therefore, after the old debts are resolved, it can proceed to develop China's railway network, so that China's vast areas can trade with foreign countries, which is most mutually beneficial to China and Britain. In addition to the long-term credit required for railway construction, attention should be paid to the methods of obtaining medium-term credit at this time. This type of credit is especially beneficial to the operation of public utilities. During my months in China, I deeply admired the efforts of municipal authorities in various places in municipal construction. I think British manufacturers and exporters should consult with banks and relevant government departments operating in China to assist in the implementation of reliable plans. There are also many opportunities for private capital investment in China. However, in order to attract investors' attention, discrimination against foreign investment should be eliminated to deepen foreigners' confidence. In terms of real estate, it should be fully guaranteed in terms of mortgage rights. If it is treated unfairly, foreign investment will definitely not be able to help China. I fully agree with the American Economic Survey Mission's statement that China is currently undergoing a huge change. I believe that the result of this change will make China a more effective place for British commercial, industrial and financial operations. The main concern of Britain to China is to increase China's prosperity and trade, and to maintain its peace. If we work hard on this, the beneficiaries will not only be Britain, but also countries around the world that trade with China. China's construction is intricate, and our country wants to help, and we can do our best everywhere. Although the Chinese government is in the midst of hardships, it has made amazing progress in developing transportation, revitalizing rural areas, and restoring safety and order. The recent currency reform is especially well-managed, and its success will benefit everyone. Finally, before the end, I would like to express my deep gratitude on behalf of my colleagues to the Chinese government and Chinese and foreign banks and businessmen for the assistance they have given us.

The National Products Preservation Association Petitions for the Announcement of the Abolition of the Boxer Protocol

The Chinese National Products Preservation Association yesterday submitted a petition to the National Government's Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting the announcement of the abolition of the Boxer Protocol to maintain security in North China. The original text reads: To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government, President Jiang of the Executive Yuan, and Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as reported, Japan is using the Boxer Protocol as an excuse to increase its troops in North China for no reason. Its ulterior motives are obvious. According to the main purpose of the Boxer Protocol, one is to compensate various countries for military expenses, and the other is to maintain transportation in Tianjin and protect embassies. Therefore, various countries are allowed to station troops in appropriate sections. Today, as times have changed, the above two items have completely failed in fact. Since the establishment of the Republic of China, countries that have strengthened friendly relations have all returned the Boxer Indemnity. This means that the agreement has failed and should be announced for abolition. First, our government has established its capital in Nanjing. Ambassadors and ministers from various friendly countries have all moved south with the capital for convenience, or have chosen to work in Beijing and Shanghai. In reality, the embassy in Beijing is only a part of the building. This means that the agreement has failed and should be announced for abolition. Secondly, in order to maintain sovereignty and prevent disputes, the Association dares to make a bold request and send a special telegram. We respectfully request that your government, the Yuan, and the Ministry quickly abolish the Boxer Protocol in accordance with the facts, and inform the friendly countries listed in the agreement in order to maintain sovereignty and prevent excuses. We await your orders with trepidation. The Standing Committee of the Chinese National Products Preservation Association, Wang Jie'an, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqi, respectfully kowtow.

Currently, the way to save the country is only to promote national products, and there is no other appropriate way. I hope that the guests attending the meeting will share this purpose, spread the word, and provide more assistance, so as to achieve twice the result with half the effort, he said. Then, Liu Zhongying gave a speech, omitting the details.

Fire Extinguishing Demonstration At 4 PM, the Puqiu Industrial Company demonstrated fire extinguishers and fire extinguishing bombs in Penglai Garden. A wooden house was built in the field. First, flammable materials were sprinkled, and then the fire was lit. The demonstration included: 1. Shooting power test of chemical fire extinguisher; 2. Shooting power test of foam fire extinguisher; 3. Foam volume expansion test; Wood frame fire test; 5. Oil pool fire; 6. Wood house fire. Among them, the foam fire extinguisher was the most effective. When the wooden house was on fire, the fire extinguishing bomb was tested. After three bombs were thrown, the fire remained. It was still extinguished by the foam fire extinguisher. Compared with the performers of the Da Zhong last year, it was much inferior.

Lantern Parade The manufacturers of the National Exhibition also held a lantern parade at 6 PM. More than 100 factories and more than 1,000 lanterns participated. First, they set off from Penglai Road and walked along Zhonghua Road, Xiaoximen, Dananmen, Xiaonanmen, Dadongmen, Xiaodongmen, Renminguo Road, Xinkaihe, Laobeimen, Xinbeimen, Xinqiaojie, Fangbang Bridge, Ximen, and then to Penglai Road to disband. The crowd along the way was blocked.

Promotional Program The National Products Promotion Mobilization opened yesterday and will last until the 28th. The program today is the National Products Factory Promotion Day. Various national products groups will lead manufacturers to hold trademark sample exhibitions. Tomorrow (24th) is Student Promotion Day. Each school will conduct clothing inspections separately and hold sample exhibitions. The 25th is Industrial Promotion Day. The General Trade Union will lead separate national products promotion conferences. The 26th is Recreational Promotion Day. Movie theaters will add slide shows and broadcast on the radio. Various entertainers will give interspersed speeches. The 27th is Group Promotion Day. All groups in the city will be mobilized to post slogans. The 28th is Citizen Promotion Day. The citizens' associations in the two special districts will lead citizens to promote separately. The National Exhibition will also close on that day, it is said.
